The Issue Between the Municipal Council and Rickshaw Owners Is Becoming Increasingly Serious 135

Rickshaw Owners Association to Hold General Meeting Today

City Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter Requesting Attention to the Case

Municipal Council Declares No Change in Attitude

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, after the Public Concession Municipal Council's Rickshaw Management Committee issued new regulations for licensing, the rickshaw owners petitioned for improvements due to the difficulties in implementation. The Management Committee did not allow this. Hua Dong Yu Qiaqing and Jiang-Huai Fellow Townsmen Association Cheng Xiechun, considering that the rickshaw industry is related to the livelihood of 100,000 civilians, warned that if problems were to arise, they would inevitably lead to disturbances. Together, they requested the Management Committee to extend the deadline to allow for proper planning, but this was rejected by the Management Committee. Therefore, the two sides have formed a stalemate. According to the Municipal Council's Information Office, the Municipal Council has received applications from new rickshaw owners for licenses. However, according to the Xinsheng News Agency's investigation, even with a license issued by the Public Concession alone, it is impossible to obtain approval from the Concession's Chinese authorities. In fact, it is still difficult to operate. The details are recorded below:

Association Requests Assistance from Various Organizations, According to the Xinxin News Agency, the Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association's Special District Office yesterday, regarding the Public Concession Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Management Committee's implementation of new regulations, separately submitted petitions to the Taxpaying Chinese Association, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Jiang-Huai Fellow Townsmen Association, and various fellow townsmen associations, requesting them to forward letters to the Board of Directors of the Bureau, requesting that the treatment be improved during the reconsideration of the new regulations, as a final remedy. The original letter stated: We respectfully inform you that the former Rickshaw Committee of the Municipal Council made sixteen reform proposals for the rickshaw industry. The Board of Directors resolved thirteen of these, establishing a Rickshaw Affairs Management Committee, which would make various changes to the licensing procedures for the rickshaw industry. Our association has repeatedly sent representatives to petition, requesting that the difficulties of merchants be considered, but this was not approved. The Taxpaying Association also sent a letter to the Bureau, requesting that it be given serious consideration. Recently, Hua Dong Yu Qiaqing and Mr. Cheng Xiechun, a standing committee member of your association, went to discuss the matter in person, requesting an extension of the deadline, but to no avail. In this way, without any regard for whether the rickshaw industry can be maintained, the Bureau is determined to have its own way. Its destructive policies, such as reforming the rickshaw design, reducing rickshaw fares, collecting monthly mutual aid fees, and abolishing the right to inherit licenses, have been announced to take effect from August 1st, causing rickshaw owners' businesses to be unsustainable. In that case, the livelihoods of over 100,000 rickshaw pullers and their families in this city will inevitably be ruined, and the public order in the concession will be seriously affected. If this is extended from the rickshaw industry to other industries, wouldn't all Chinese merchants in the Public Concession who have licenses be in danger? Our association has already submitted a petition to the Board of Directors of the Bureau, requesting reconsideration. In addition to sending separate letters requesting assistance, we have always admired your association as the leader of our hometown, upholding justice. Therefore, we have specially attached a copy of the reasons for requesting reconsideration, and we respectfully request that you consider our suffering and approve another letter to the Board of Directors of the Bureau, requesting that the treatment be improved during the reconsideration, as the final relief, so as to avoid bankruptcy. Not only will the rickshaw industry and the hundreds of thousands of rickshaw pullers be fortunate, but also the protection of various industries will be significant. We hope for your understanding.

The City Chamber of Commerce writes to the Municipal Council, The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has received a report from representatives of the Rickshaw Industry Association, stating that the Public Concession's regulations for managing the rickshaw industry are seriously detrimental to the industry and the lives of over 100,000 rickshaw pullers and their families, as well as the rickshaw manufacturing industry. According to the association's proposals: (1) Rickshaw licenses should be issued according to the Rice Industry Association's method, in order to save the Municipal Council's expenses and reduce the burden on taxpayers. (2) The rickshaw industry should be changed into a specialized public utility, with corresponding rights and obligations. (3) If the Municipal Council's duty is to provide relief to rickshaw pullers, it should start by maintaining the rickshaw industry. If the current proposed method is implemented, the rickshaw industry will inevitably cease to exist, and the rickshaw pullers who rely on this livelihood and their families, numbering over 100,000 people, will also be in despair. Based on this, the City Chamber of Commerce has forwarded a letter to the Municipal Council, requesting that attention be paid to the case.

Rickshaw Owners to Hold General Meeting Today The Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association's Special District Rickshaw Owners' General Meeting issued a notice stating: Regarding the implementation of the new licensing regulations by the Rickshaw Management Committee of the Municipal Council from August 1st, which is destroying the rickshaw industry and pushing it to the brink of bankruptcy, we have repeatedly received requests from various rickshaw owners. Our office has repeatedly sent personnel to explain the difficulties of the rickshaw industry, hoping for improvements. We have also submitted a petition to the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council for reconsideration, and have appealed to the City Chamber of Commerce, the Taxpaying Chinese Association, and various industry organizations to provide assistance. However, until yesterday, the Board of Directors' proposal on this case still yielded no results. As the licensing period is approaching, a special emergency general meeting of rickshaw owners will be convened at 2:00 PM on the 27th of this month at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's auditorium, located at Tianhou Palace Bridge, to jointly discuss licensing methods. In addition to publishing a notice in the newspaper, we specially notify your members to check and immediately inform all rickshaw owners to attend the discussion. The matter is urgent, so we hope that you will attend the meeting at that time. This is to notify you.

The Municipal Council Issues News According to the news released by the Municipal Council's Information Office, the Municipal Council recently announced that a large number of rickshaw owners have not complied with the Bureau's regulations to apply for rickshaw owner certificates. If they fail to apply by the deadline, the licenses will be suspended or new people will be recruited to take over. After the rickshaw owners' association petitioned, the deadline for applying for rickshaw owner certificates was extended to July 30th. However, after the extension, not many people have applied. At the same time, the Rickshaw Affairs Committee announced that if the number of applications from existing rickshaw owners is insufficient, the committee will receive new applications from July 25th to 29th, or existing rickshaw owners who are willing to comply with the regulations and want to expand their business may also apply. As of the evening of the 25th, the committee had received 1,581 applications, with a total of 12,641 licenses applied for. Applicants, whether individuals or companies, have stated that they are willing to abide by all new regulations. When distributing licenses in the future, those who are willing to cooperate in promoting the rickshaw pullers' mutual aid association plan will be given priority.

Rickshaw Pullers' Relief Association's Attitude Furthermore, according to the Municipal Council's Information Office, approximately 2,000 rickshaw pullers in the Public Concession, in the name of the Rickshaw Pullers' Relief Association, jointly submitted a petition to the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Committee, expressing their unanimous support for the committee's reform plan. The petition stated, "Regarding the methods agreed upon by your committee: (1) From August 1st, rickshaw fares will be reduced to 10 cents, plus a 1-cent relief fee, for a total of 11 cents for two shifts per day. (2) From January 1st of next year, fares will be further reduced to 8 cents, plus a 1-cent relief fee, for a total of 9 cents (3) Free registration will be handled by the Relief Association. The above points are approved by the association and unanimously supported by 2,000 representatives. However, the rickshaw style will be determined by your committee. In short, regarding any undertaking that benefits our rickshaw pullers, we rickshaw pullers pledge to be your strong support. We also request that your committee send someone to take charge and lead so that the Relief Association can be established as soon as possible. We are deeply grateful." The rickshaw pullers also sent representatives to the committee to explain everything and express their attitude.

Proceeds from Municipal Bonds Delivered to the Finance Bureau by the Bank of China 136

Xinfeng Trading Company Receives Commission of 175,000

Supervisory Committee for Various Projects to Be Established

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, the 3.5 million yuan in Shanghai Municipal Bonds issued in 1934 were underwritten by the Xinfeng Trading Company and sold to the public. After the full amount was sold, the proceeds have been delivered to the Finance Bureau by the Bank of China. A supervisory committee for the commencement of various construction projects will be organized. Details are recorded below:

Proceeds Fully Delivered 137

The 3.5 million yuan in municipal bonds were underwritten by a syndicate organized by the American Xinfeng Trading Company at 93% of the face value. Among them, 1.5 million yuan were purchased by the underwriting syndicate itself, and 2 million yuan were sold to the public by the distributing Bank of China at 98% of the face value. The entire amount was sold immediately and was oversubscribed by six times the total amount, which was allocated proportionally. The proceeds from the bonds, calculated at the underwriting price of 93%, totaled 3,255,000 yuan, which was delivered to the Municipal Finance Bureau by the Bank of China with a check issued the day before. The underwriting commission of 5%, totaling 175,000 yuan, was also delivered to Xinfeng Trading Company by the Bank of China.

Supervisory Committee to Be Organized 138

The municipal government will use the proceeds from the issuance of municipal bonds for projects such as improving roads and bridges, constructing museums, libraries, hospitals, sports fields, and slaughterhouses, in accordance with the approved original plan. As for the supervisory committee organized to supervise the use of funds, the municipal government has sent letters to various agencies to recommend representatives to jointly organize it. The members include the Director of the Finance Bureau, the Director of the Public Works Bureau, the Director of the Education Bureau, the National Debt Fund Management Committee, the Provisional Municipal Assembly, the Shanghai Bankers' Association, and Xinfeng Trading Company, totaling seven people. Once the representatives are nominated, a meeting will be held to announce its establishment.

Shanghai Representative Returns from National Traffic Police Improvement Conference 140

Li Mu Discusses Conference Details

In order to unify and improve traffic police administration nationwide, the Ministry of Interior recently convened a National Traffic Police Conference in Beijing. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau specially sent Secretary Li Mu to attend. Mr. Li returned to Shanghai yesterday. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Li to inquire about the conference proceedings. According to Mr. Li,

Participants in the conference included representatives from the public security bureaus of Hubei, Fujian, Guangdong, Shandong, Hebei, Zhejiang, and other provinces, as well as representatives from the public security bureaus of Tianjin, Beijing, Qingdao, Hankou, Shanghai, and other cities, and representatives from the Capital Police Department, totaling thirty-two people. Li Songfeng, Director of the Police Administration Department of the Ministry of Interior, presided over everything. There were three general meetings and three review meetings, and the results were very satisfactory.

Key Conference Issues Mr. Li also said that there were a total of thirty-two proposals, divided into four groups: organization, training, command, and reorganization. As the traffic industry is developing rapidly, traffic police administration is becoming more important. Therefore, the representatives were very attentive during the discussions. The two most important cases were the unified command and traffic knowledge training. Regarding the first case, because the traffic control agencies in various places were not unified, various difficulties often arose. Therefore, in the future, the Ministry of Interior will request the central government to instruct all provinces and cities to have traffic control handled by the police administration agencies. As for the traffic knowledge training case, it will be divided into two steps: one for the traffic police to start with, and one for the public to start with. On the public side, film propaganda will be used and incorporated into textbooks. It is also planned to hold a safety week so that the general public can understand traffic issues.

After the Successful Loan for the Yuping Railway, the Contract Has Been Agreed Upon and Will Soon Be Signed 144

The Representative of the Lending Syndicate Is the Bank of China

The Loan Will Be Repaid Within Five Years After the Completion of the Railway

The Ministry of Railways and other institutions mortgaged 16 million yuan of the First Phase Railway Construction Bonds and Yuping Railway Bonds, each worth 12 million yuan, to the Bank of China, the Central Bank, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and other banks in Shanghai, as well as the Four Banks Savings Association. Half of this amount, 8 million yuan, will be used as a guarantee for merchants purchasing building materials for the Yuping Railway. The interest rate is 7.5%. The loan will be repaid within five years after the completion of the railway. The draft contract has been signed. As for the formal contract, revisions have been agreed upon, and it will be signed by the Bank of China, the representative of the syndicate formed by the borrowing banks, and the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Railways, the Jiangxi Provincial Government, and the merchants purchasing materials.

City Chamber of Commerce Revises Rules for Accepting Cases 145

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a report to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating: Regarding the petition for the matter, Article 3, Section 2, of the Chamber's articles of association stipulates: "For items 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, and 11 of the preceding paragraph, fees may be charged at the discretion of the local competent government after approval by the local competent government." Article 9, Section 10, states: "When members entrust the Chamber of Commerce to handle items 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, and 11 of Article 3 of these articles of association, they shall enjoy the right to free or reduced fees." According to the above provisions, only events handled by members can be free or reduced fees, and non-members should pay, so as to distinguish between them. Therefore, according to this purpose, eleven rules for accepting cases were drawn up in September 1930. For non-members requesting handling of events, the amount of fees was determined, and a report was submitted to your Bureau for record in the same year in September and implemented since then. In light of the situation, the original office fee of 30 yuan per case was fixed, and the amount was lost, and facts inevitably hindered it. Also, if the requester's own business already has a public association organization, the reason is to join the industry association in accordance with Article 7 of the Law on Industry Associations. If they are allowed to directly pay the fee when something happens and entrust the Chamber to handle it, it is tantamount to supporting that they do not need to join the association, which is also inconsistent with the provisions of Article 7 of the law. It was then proposed to summarize the meaning of Article 9 under the original text of Article 5 of the rules for non-members requesting events, and modify it to be reviewed by the Chamber. If the industry does not have a public association organization and cannot legally join the public association, and the request does belong to the scope of commercial affairs, the Chamber may charge office expenses at its discretion and handle it on its behalf. The original text of Article 9 was deleted, and the original text of Article 6 was added under "30 yuan per case", adding "However, in special circumstances, a reduction may be considered after verification. If the event is too cumbersome, it may be increased at the discretion of the Standing Committee of the Chamber of Commerce, and the original text of Article 7 is merged into the footnote of that article to save space." The full text of nine articles was discussed, revised, and passed at the fourth Executive Committee meeting on July 23, and is now copied in full and submitted to your Bureau for review and approval for record, which is a public convenience.

Revision of Transportation Contract for Tongji Company by Two Railways 146

Wuxi Tongji Tugboat Company previously entered into a contract with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to undertake the loading and unloading of railway-transported goods at the Wuxi railway riverbank, paying an annual wharfage fee of two hundred silver dollars. This contract expired on November 30th of the seventeenth year (of the Republic). The company continued to pay the wharfage fee without ceasing. Now, the Railway's Transportation Department, considering the actual needs, revised the contract terms item by item, submitted them to the Railway Bureau for approval, and signed the following terms on June 30th of this year: (1) The Railway Bureau allows the company to use railway-registered vessels to load and unload railway-transported goods at the Wuxi railway riverbank, but the company shall not obstruct other merchants or individuals from using their own vessels to load and unload their own goods at the riverbank. (2) The company shall have forty fully equipped tugboats and ten reserve boats, all of which must be registered with the Railway Bureau. An annual registration fee of five silver dollars per boat shall be paid, totaling two hundred and fifty yuan, to be paid in full upon the establishment of the contract. The above-mentioned boats shall be inspected by the Railway Bureau, and licenses shall be issued and affixed in a conspicuous place on the boats, not to be defaced, so that the Railway Bureau can inspect them at any time. (3) The company's rates for loading and unloading goods shall not exceed those stipulated by local businesses of the same type. Upon the establishment of the contract, the rates shall be submitted to the Railway Bureau for approval and publication. Once published, the company shall not arbitrarily change them. If changes are necessary, the company shall obtain the consent of the Railway Bureau. Outside the stipulated rates, the company shall not solicit anything from customers. If there is any solicitation, the Railway Bureau shall be free to impose penalties. (4) The company shall strictly abide by all existing and future regulations issued by the Railway Bureau and shall be responsible for guaranteeing the conduct of all its employees within the railway premises. (5) The company shall provide a security deposit of one thousand national currency dollars and a guarantee from a reputable firm, to be deposited with the Railway Bureau as a guarantee of compliance with this contract. This guarantee and security deposit shall be returned in full by the Railway Bureau upon the termination of the contract if the company has not violated any terms. (6) If the Railway Bureau believes that the company has any matters for improvement or reform, it may notify the company in writing. If the company fails to comply, the Railway Bureau may cancel the contract at any time. (7) The company shall be responsible for protecting any buildings of the Railway Bureau. If there is any damage, compensation shall be paid according to the value. (8) The benefits stipulated in this contract shall not be transferred without the written consent of the Railway Bureau. The Railway Bureau shall not issue licenses that conflict with the benefits of this contract to others during the valid term, in order to maintain the benefits. (9) This contract shall come into effect on July 1st of the twenty-third year of the Republic of China and shall be valid for ten months. If both parties have no objections upon expiration, it may be extended. However, this shall not apply where the terms are otherwise specified. (10) This contract shall be made in duplicate originals, with the Railway Bureau and the company each holding one copy for compliance. A duplicate copy shall also be kept by the Railway Bureau's Chief Audit Office for verification.

Measures Drafted by the Bureau of Social Affairs

Municipal Council Cautious in Issuing Driver's Licenses 149

The Municipal Council's Transportation Committee believes that under the current regulations, if a minor applies for a driver's license, they must submit a letter from their parents or guardians expressing their permission and proving that they are at least seventeen years old before a license can be issued. However, this procedure is only a regulation set by the Police Department and is not explicitly stated in the license regulations. Recently, a guardian certificate submitted by a minor applicant was found to be false. Since there is no explicit provision in the regulations, it is difficult to deal with the situation. After discussion, it was decided to add a clause to the driver's license regulations stating that if an applicant knowingly makes a false statement, their license may be withheld or revoked. This proposal was approved by the Board of Directors, and it was stipulated that all applicants for driver's licenses must comply with this clause.

Rambling Talk on Yangzhou: China Bookstore Proposes Mediation Terms 150

Yangzhou Natives in Shanghai Considering

Central News Agency reports that the China Bookstore's publication of "Rambling Talk on Yangzhou" by Mr. Yi Junzuo, Director of the Editorial Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, has aroused public anger among the people of Yangzhou. Yangzhou natives residing abroad have organized committees to investigate "Rambling Talk on Yangzhou" in various places in response. Mr. Lu Feikui, General Manager of the China Bookstore, has entrusted a friend to invite lawyer Xue Dubi to mediate. Previously, Mr. Xue visited Shanghai-based Yangzhou lawyer Shan Yuhua and Shanghai-based Yangzhou native Ruan Mubai, stating the China Bookstore's willingness to: 1. Publish an apology to the people of Yangzhou in the newspaper; 2. Stop selling "Rambling Talk on Yangzhou" in the China Bookstore's main store and branches; 3. Donate all proceeds from the sale of "Rambling Talk on Yangzhou" to purchase summer medicines for distribution in Yangzhou; 4. Donate several types of books published by the China Bookstore to the Yangzhou Library. However, Shan Yuhua and Ruan Mubai believe that the matter is significant and that it would be difficult to accept the mediation terms without the consent of all the Yangzhou natives. They only agreed to submit the proposed mediation terms to the Yangzhou Eight Counties Association in Shanghai. At 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, the Yangzhou Eight Counties Association in Shanghai convened a meeting of committee members to discuss the matter. Those present included Shen Dingchen, Hou Dachun, Song Shixiang, Li Zhixi, Jiao Dingkai, Hua Zhijing, Qian Shusheng, Liu Yongque, Hang Shijun, Zhu Xinong, Qian Cangshuo, Ai Guofan, Ruan Mubai, Ruan Lianzhong, etc. After discussion, it was decided to submit the mediation terms proposed by the China Bookstore to the Yangzhou natives' committee in Shanghai investigating the book "Rambling Talk on Yangzhou" for detailed consideration. Retrial Verdict for Liu Chongwu and Others

Liu Sentenced to Seven Years, Pan and Tian Each Sentenced to Six Years

Cao Songshou Sentenced to Twelve Years for Conspiracy to Murder

Patriotic youths Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, Tian Shuiyang, and others, previously organized a patriotic group in light of the brutality of the Japanese invaders. They sent letters warning Shanghai merchants not to purchase enemy goods, but the result was ineffective. They then carried out intimidation, shooting and killing Wang Zhengtao, the owner of Maotai Foreign Goods Store on Xinza Road, and throwing bombs as a warning. After the incident, the police arrested Liu and the other four and handed them over to the First Special Court, imposing light punishments on each of them. However, the police were dissatisfied and appealed. The Second Branch of the High Court heard the case and sentenced Liu, Pan, and Cao to twelve years of imprisonment each for continuous joint conspiracy to murder, and Tian Shuiyang to six years of imprisonment. The defendants, upon hearing the verdict, declared their dissatisfaction and hired lawyers to appeal to the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court, after carefully examining the case, found that there were still doubts in the case and sent the case back to the Second Branch of the High Court for retrial. The retrial has now concluded, and a sentence was scheduled to be announced. The circumstances of the sentences have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the verdict was announced by President Yu Hua, accompanied by judges Zhao and Jiang. The main text of the verdict reads: The original verdict regarding Liu Chongwu's possession of military firearms and ammunition and the portions concerning Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, and Tian Shuiyang are revoked. Liu Chongwu is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for continuous joint intention to use military firearms and ammunition for criminal purposes, combined with the original sentence for murder, the executed imprisonment shall be seven years. The appeal of the other parts is dismissed. Pan Hongsheng and Tian Shuiyang are each sentenced to six years of imprisonment for assisting in the conspiracy to murder. Cao Songshou is sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for jointly conspiring to murder. The number of days of detention before the judgment is final shall be converted to one day for every two days of imprisonment. Five pistols and forty-four rounds of ammunition are confiscated.

Allow Separation of Good and Bad in Suppressing Street Vendors

Resolution of Street Vendor Dispute 155

The Local Goods Industry and Market Association Requested the Municipal Council Yesterday

The Local Goods Stores Resumed Business Simultaneously from 3:00 PM

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that after the street vendors in this city stopped hawking from the day before yesterday, they also caused trouble near the local goods stores, causing the melons sold by the local goods stores to be unsellable. Yesterday, the Local Goods Industry Association sent four representatives to petition the Municipal Council, and the Standing Committee of the Citizens' Federation also went to the Municipal Council to request the suppression of street vendors by separating good and bad. The authorities agreed to instruct the Police Department to comply. All parties resumed business at 3:00 PM. The details of the process are as follows:

Reason for Stopping Hawking 156

The street vendors who hawk along the streets, especially those who hawk silk stockings, undershirts, and children's clothing, often work in groups of three or four in places like Fourth Malu, Daxin Street, and Fifth Malu. However, because their business is dishonest, when they encounter simple-minded customers who use large coins to pay, they make excuses and even run away on the pretext of "the police are coming." Therefore, they are unpopular and reported to the police station, requesting suppression. The police authorities immediately dispatched police officers to arrest and punish them indiscriminately, regardless of whether they are good or bad. The street vendors selling fruits are greatly affected because they are carrying heavy loads and have difficulty escaping. This led to the smashing of melons bought by customers near the local goods stores, causing buyers to hesitate. Yesterday morning, these street vendors were still scattered in places such as Lao Zha Bridge and the Sixteen Shops, waiting to carry out their sabotage work. Therefore, the local goods stores at Lao Zha Bridge have all temporarily suspended business. All the river boats carrying melons that have not been loaded have sailed to other places to sell, and those whose goods have already been loaded can only wait for a solution. Boats on the way have also reportedly turned to other places.

Great Losses 157

There are a total of sixteen local goods stores in Lao Zha, including Long Shun, Qu Futai, Yuji, Yongchang, Yida, Zhengtai, Yuanda, Tongcheng, Longyuanshun, Shengchang, Changtai, Yongshun, Yongchang, Yongsheng, Xieda, and Yujixing. Each store can sell more than 1,500 yuan per day, totaling more than 20,000 yuan per day. There are about 2,000 porters, each earning 2 yuan per day, totaling 4,000 yuan. There are also hundreds of foremen who can earn more than 1,000 yuan per day for unloading and delivering goods. All are greatly affected by the disturbance.

Petition Yesterday Morning 158

The local goods stores believe that although they can sustain themselves despite the losses, the porters and foremen rely on their daily income to make a living. If this stalemate continues, it will inevitably lead to incidents. Therefore, they sent representatives Ma Shangde, Cao Quanlin, Zhou Shenyan, and Yang Guanqi as representatives to petition the Municipal Council. The councilor He Dekui received them. After the representatives stated their intentions, Council He immediately stated that the street vendors had also come to request. Therefore, he has now informed the Police Department that if they encounter legitimate businesses, they will be lenient, and it can be resolved in a day or two. The representatives were satisfied and left. This afternoon, the Local Goods Industry Association also issued leaflets to persuade the street vendors to resume business as usual. The Municipal Council has agreed to be lenient and exempt them from prosecution.

Request for Relief 159

Street vendor representatives Li Maoting, Geng Dashou, Bao Guizhi, Xue Delong, and others submitted a petition to the First Special District Citizens' Federation yesterday afternoon, requesting relief and making a second petition. Standing Committee member Zhang Yichen received them and agreed to forward the request to the Municipal Council for proper solutions. Zhang Yichen immediately went to the Municipal Council and explained the plight of the street vendors to Councilor He Dekui, emphasizing the need to protect their livelihoods and to strictly suppress the bad elements at any time. Councilor He agreed to convey the message to the chief officer to notify the Police Department to conduct a thorough investigation and suppress them separately. The good street vendors will be treated leniently. Representative Zhang was satisfied and left. He then informed the respective street vendor representatives to resume business as usual to maintain their livelihoods.

Resumption of Trade 160

Municipal Council member He Dekui, after receiving the petition representatives from the local goods industry in the morning and consulting with the chief officer, agreed to be accommodating. He specially summoned both parties for talks. Yang Guanqi, Ma Shangde, Cao Quanlin, and Zhou Shenyan from the local goods industry, and Cai Shuqing, Hong Azu, Xu Agen, and other street vendor representatives, went to the Municipal Council at 2:00 PM to meet with Councilor He Dekui. According to Councilor He, the good street vendors will continue to be treated as usual, and there will be no strict suppression. If unscrupulous elements take the opportunity to use illegal business practices to extort money, the authorities will investigate and severely punish them. The good street vendors can do business with peace of mind. The representatives were satisfied. Therefore, the turmoil subsided at 3:00 PM. The local goods stores resumed business as usual, and the street vendors also hawked their goods without interfering with each other.

Notice of Resumption of Business 161

The Shanghai Local Goods Industry Association hereby notifies all street vendors to resume business immediately. The association has sent representatives to contact the Municipal Council regarding the dispute over the closure of business by various street vendors. The Municipal Council's Council He Dekui stated that the livelihood of street vendors should be taken into account. It is hoped that all law-abiding street vendors will resume business as usual and continue to operate as before, without strict suppression. However, if there are unscrupulous elements who take the opportunity to incite disturbances, the authorities must investigate and punish them severely, which has nothing to do with the good street vendors. Therefore, the case has been resolved satisfactorily. Therefore, this notice is issued to all street vendors, hoping that they will resume business immediately to secure their livelihoods and end the dispute. This is most earnestly hoped for.

Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 162

Central News Agency reports that the daily necessities industry and all street vendors in this city, through the Second Branch of the First Special District Citizens' Federation, sent a letter to the Police Department of the Public Concession, stating that the street vendors often engage in fraudulent acts and requesting that they be suppressed in order to seek redress. Yesterday, they specially sent representatives Li Maoting and others to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to request assistance in order to prevent their livelihood from being cut off. The original letter is excerpted as follows: Due to being unjustly detained and fined, they are unable to operate and their livelihood is on the verge of being cut off, we appeal to your association to uphold justice and provide relief. We have always been engaged in selling daily necessities of national goods as a business, setting up stalls to sell and earn a small profit to maintain our lives and operate lawfully. Recently, the Second Branch of the First Special District Citizens' Federation in Shanghai stated that we cheat and extort money, induce people to buy, and cause disputes, etc., and sent a letter to the Police Department of the Municipal Council to strictly suppress us and evict us. We have investigated that this situation is due to the fact that those who sell children's shirts and silk stockings are rampant in cheating. As for us, we have always been lawful and dare not cheat. Once we encounter a patrolman, we are immediately detained and fined, and some are even fined three or four times a day, so that we cannot do business. Our eight-member family relies on this for a living. If this continues, our hundreds of street vendors and thousands of families will all starve to death. The Citizens' Federation was originally intended to protect the citizens and uphold justice. We are all citizens of Shanghai, but not only have we not been protected, but we have been oppressed. The original letter referred to cheating and extortion, but failed to distinguish between good and bad and added misfortune to us, which is difficult to accept. We believe that our transactions with people are fair in price, and the establishment of a sale is based on the consent of both parties. How can we force it? If there is fraud, the authorities can investigate and punish us according to the law. This kind of action by the association is contrary to law and human feelings. We have been appealing for help since we were driven away. We believe that your association leads the commercial community, advocates justice, and has the purpose of helping the poor and the distressed. We have decided to send Li Maoting, Geng Dashou, Bao Guizhi, Xue Delong, and others as temporary representatives of all the street vendors selling daily necessities of national goods to submit a petition, requesting your audience and allowing the following opinions: (1) Request to forward a letter to the Police Department of the Municipal Council, granting leniency and allowing us to live. (2) Request to order the Second Branch of the First Special District Citizens' Federation to treat all citizens equally in the future. If they express opinions, they should seriously advocate them to avoid criticism and provide for life. We dare to ask you to intercede on our behalf, and we will be grateful for the rest of our lives. We are anxiously awaiting your orders.

Hospital Director Disappearance Case Resembles Kidnapping 166

A Car Suddenly Abducted the Director

The Inside Story is Full of Mysteries, the Truth Unknown

The Dongwu Hospital at 99 Jing'an Temple Road was founded by Chen Zhenya. However, in the early stages, due to lack of funds, he required staff to pay a certain amount of guarantee money when recruiting them. Ostensibly called a "guarantee," this money was actually used for starting the hospital and purchasing all necessary equipment. Unexpectedly, since its opening, business has been slow, making it difficult for Chen to maintain the hospital, and he has accumulated debts of over eight thousand yuan. The hospital staff discovered this, and collectively demanded repayment of their guarantee money. Chen Zhenya had no choice but to offset the debt with all the hospital's assets to settle with the staff. However, he was unable to compensate the apprentice guarantee money and the hospital's external creditors. Therefore, the creditors filed a lawsuit in court. Chen also hired lawyer Jin Zhi, who resided in Hengmao Lane, Baxianqiao, to handle the case. Meanwhile, the creditors appointed staff to stay in the hospital and monitor Chen's movements. Unexpectedly, at around 7:00 AM yesterday, a Feiyun automobile suddenly sped to the hospital entrance. Three people were inside. After getting out of the car, they went straight into the hospital, claiming to be detectives from the police station, ordered to arrest Chen. They immediately escorted Chen into the car and drove away, appearing flustered and disoriented. The hospital staff became suspicious, especially since the car was not an official police vehicle, which made them believe it was a kidnapping case. They quickly reported it to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, requesting an investigation. After receiving the news, the police station sent detectives to investigate the Feiyun Automobile Company. According to the driver, they had been taken to the entrance of Hengmao Lane, near the Baxianqiao Small Vegetable Market in the French Concession. The police then followed various clues to investigate, but returned without results. Although they inquired at the office of lawyer Jin Zhi in Hengmao Lane, Jin Zhi claimed to know absolutely nothing about it. Therefore, the police believe there is another story behind this case and further investigation and verification is needed.

Shishan Lane Rent Reduction Dispute Resolved 167

Meeting Held Yesterday to Report Negotiation Results

The Shishan Lane Rent Reduction Branch of the Sixth District Citizens' Association held a meeting yesterday at 8:00 PM at its clubhouse to discuss with all the tenants. Over 80 people attended, including Qiu Jialiang, Yang Jingcai, and Zhou Fuzhang. Qiu Jialiang was elected as chairman. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and the results of the three negotiations with Xiangmao Foreign Firm. The foreign firm has sent a letter agreeing to a rent reduction with three specific measures: (1) Storefronts along the road will be granted a 20% rent reduction as requested. However, due to different conditions, the rent for residences within the lane will be reduced from 37 yuan to 32 yuan, and from 35 yuan to 30 yuan. But the water bill will be the responsibility of the tenants. (2) Old rent arrears up to April of this year must be paid in full. Any remaining arrears will be paid monthly according to the old and new rates until cleared. (3) The rent reduction period will be from July of this year to the end of June next year. After the expiration, the situation will be reviewed and further consultation will take place. If there were previous deposits made in the bank, each tenant should withdraw the money from the bank to settle the arrears. The tenants considered this satisfactory and unanimously approved it on the spot. The meeting adjourned without discussing other matters.

Brutal Daughter-in-Law Offends Mother-in-Law, Who Angrily Commits Suicide by Poisoning 168

Son Returns Home from Work

Old Mother Groaning in Bed

The old woman Sun Wang, a native of Funing, residing at No. 201 Dongyouheng Road, is 65 years old. She has three grown sons. The second son, Liansheng, works as a driver in the tram company. His wife, Zhou, is extremely fierce. If the mother-in-law slightly disagrees with her, Zhou would quarrel with her. The day before yesterday, Zhou had a big argument with the mother-in-law over trivial household matters, which was heard by the neighbors. The old woman became increasingly resentful and had the thought of ending her life. She secretly swallowed opium to commit suicide. When her son returned home from work at 3:00 PM, he saw his mother groaning in bed. When asked, she did not reveal the truth. So, he took her to Tongren Hospital and then transferred her to Guangren Hospital. The medical treatment was ineffective, and she died. The hospital reported it to the Jiaxing Road Police Station, who ordered Detective Liu Zongcheng to investigate. The body was then moved to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Judge Guo Wei of the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to examine the body. According to Detective Liu Zongcheng's report of the situation, Judge Guo determined that the deceased Liu Wang, a female, had indeed died from opium poisoning before her death. The body was handed over to her son, Sun Liansheng, to be claimed for burial after signing an affidavit.

Repeatedly Committing Murder and Robbery

Record of Trial of Notorious Bandits 169

Detectives Testify to the Case Cracking Circumstances

The Penglai Bank in the Penglai Market of this city was robbed on the morning of May 8th of this year, with more than 500 yuan stolen. Afterwards, team leader Gu Liancheng of the Detective Team, along with detectives Shen Jinchu, Hu Kui Sheng, Ma Wenlin, and others, first arrested the suspect Zhang San and accomplice Ma Qinxiang at the Zhang Mingji's broker store on Nancang Street and took them to the team. After interrogation by Team Leader Lu, it was learned that the accomplices were hiding in room 46 of the Yuelai Hotel in Mantingfang. Therefore, team leader Gu Liancheng again led detectives Shen Jinchu and others disguised as hotel staff, successively arresting a large number of 18 bandits, seizing three pistols, one hand grenade, one axe, one iron chisel, and three rolls of lead wire used for tying people. They were taken to the team and interrogated. The seven bandits who robbed the Penglai Bank were completely apprehended, including Li Ziyun (aka Xiao Genfa), Fan Jinsheng (aka Wei Gengsheng), Zhang San, Yang Xingen, Shen Haishan (aka Shen Xingsheng), Wu Changsheng, and Lu Jinquan (aka Que Genliang). (The Lu offender was taken away by the First Court of the Special District for another case, sentenced to four years, and has not yet been brought back.) Also apprehended were those who robbed Tang Ziyun's property at No. 51 Dasheng Lane on April 30th, the Yichun Company at No. 9 Fuchang Lane, Xiaodongmen on June 9th, Zhang Baosen's house at No. 8 Heng'an Lane at the Nanyang Bridge intersection on June 10th, the Jin family in the Northern Qingyuan Township, Ertu, Nanhui Zhagang, and the bandit Li Yunxiang, Wang A'er, Wang Meiying, Zhu Fa'er, Chen Hongsheng, Chen Guansheng, Guo Bingjin, Huang Liangqing, Ge Yousheng, Chen Alin, Chen Sandi, and Tang Amao who shot and killed Team Leader Zhu of the Nanhui County Public Security Bureau. In total, twenty bandits were apprehended. The bandits confessed that on the night of June 12th, they had discussed in room 46 of the Yuelai Hotel the intention to rob the silver box of the Jiading Bank, which was transported by an old truck. The bandits called the iron box a "steel tortoise". The hand grenade seized, according to the bandits, was to be thrown if pursuers came during the robbery of the "steel tortoise". The detective team recorded the confessions and sent them to the Third Section for transfer to the local court for strict investigation. Prosecutor Lei Binzhang reviewed the case one by one and ordered the suspects to be detained separately. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Lei ordered the team leader Gu Liancheng and detectives Shen Jinchu, Hu Kui Sheng, and Ma Wenlin, who handled the case, to appear in court to testify about the case cracking. He also ordered the suspects Zhang San, Yang Xingen, and others in custody to be brought to court for questioning for a long time. As a result, all the defendants were remanded in custody pending further investigation.

The First Five Letters Were Mistakenly Delivered Due to the Same Address

Cao Shifang's Tobacco Shop Closed Down, Became a Bandit

Zhang Tongjun, a Ningbo native residing at No. 1, First Lane, Xinkang Lane, Yangzhou Road, works as an accounting clerk at the Ewo Yarn Factory. Shen also reported to the police station. At 3:20 AM the day before yesterday, Hua Detective Xie Wanqi and Detective Tang Pengfei were waiting near Shen's residence when they caught Cao Shifang, a local man aged 23, just as he was about to slip a letter through the crack in the door. They arrested him and learned that he lived at No. 132 Taopeng Road. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Division of the First Special Court. The first five were mistakenly delivered, and he only found out later. Currently, the victim Shen Shengda is in Jiangxi and unable to attend the court. He asked for a postponement of the case.

When questioned, the defendant confessed that he had previously opened two tobacco and paper shops, but they had closed down, leaving him with no means to make a living, so he resorted to this strategy and asked for leniency. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered him to be remanded in custody for further review at a later date.

Retrial Record of the Chen Hongyu Assassination Case 171

Based on the Statements of Various People and the Facts

It Seems that Chen Has No Evidence of Committing a Crime

On the evening of December 15, 1928, at 7:00 PM, Chen Hongyu (aka Xiao Xing) was suddenly shot and killed in the Yinghua Morning Lane on Rubeson Road. Later, the police arrested the suspect Pan Qifang and sent him to court. After interrogation, he was sentenced to death and is currently held in prison, awaiting approval from superiors for execution. However, Pan had previously confessed that Chen Bingquan from Jiangbei was an accomplice who initiated the crime. Therefore, Detective Xiao and Wang Chengying of the Gordon Road Police Station arrested Chen and sent him to court, where he was sentenced to life imprisonment. Chen refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court. The result was that the appeal was rejected. It is now known that Chen Bingquan's wife, Chen Yan, believed that her husband had been falsely accused and hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to file a complaint with the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court issued an order to remand the case to the Second Branch of the High Court for retrial. Therefore, yesterday morning, President Yu of the High Court, along with judges Zhao and Jiang, sat in the First Criminal Court for the retrial. Attorney Wang Yaotang of the Police Station stated the case, saying that the police investigated Chen Bingquan for the crime of premeditated murder and asked for prosecution. Chen Hongwang's wife, Chen Yan, and sister, Chen Chen, testified that the deceased was at home when Pan Qifang came, called him out, and shot him, but Chen Bingquan was not seen at the scene. The arrested Pan Qifang's confession was ambiguous, not only did he not point to an accomplice, but he even denied committing the crime himself. Witness Chen Bingyang testified that Chen Bingquan was having dinner at his home when the incident happened. When questioned, Chen Bingquan firmly denied conspiring to kill Chen Hongyu. Finally, lawyer Chen Tingrui stood up to argue that based on the statements of the various witnesses and the facts, Chen Bingquan was undoubtedly framed. Since there was no sufficient evidence, he should be declared not guilty and the original verdict should be overturned. President Yu reviewed the statements and ordered Chen to be remanded in custody, pending sentencing on August 2nd.

Therefore, the number of businesses that cannot maintain themselves and close down is increasing daily. Unexpectedly, in this time of unheard pleas, they suddenly received a foreign language notice from the French Water and Electricity Company, stating that from July onwards, the fees for water and electricity meter installation and deposits will be increased. They were extremely surprised upon reading it. Water and electricity are public utilities, and their main purpose is to provide convenience to citizens. They are not like other businesses that can seek endless profits. Moreover, in this time of industrial depression, water and electricity still earn millions of yuan annually, yet they are still not satisfied and disregard the suffering of citizens by arbitrarily increasing prices in disguise. The French Municipal Council also failed to understand the current difficulties and observe the people's plight during this time of extreme economic panic and citizen burden, and rashly approved it, which lacks the spirit of cooperation between the authorities and citizens. It is even more regrettable. The merchants will never recognize this unreasonable disguised price increase in water and electricity. Therefore, they report the situation and urge the authorities to argue with the French authorities to revoke this decision, and will not stop until the goal is achieved. Please investigate and decide to send a letter to the French Municipal Council. (3) The term of office of the Executive Committee of the Second District Branch has expired, and it has not yet been re-elected. How should this be handled? The Missing Iron Barge of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Found in Haimen 175

Drifted out of Liu River Estuary by Wind and Waves

Missing for More Than Two Weeks, Now Found

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company towed an iron barge from Nanjing to Shanghai at the beginning of this month. It encountered wind at that time and was dropped at the Liu River. Unexpectedly, it was reported missing the next day. It was not found until recently. It is currently being negotiated with other ships to tow it back. The details of this matter are described as follows:

Iron Barge Missing 176

On the sixth of this month, when the Jianguo ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was awaiting orders to launch from the Yangtze River, it towed a large iron barge from Nanjing to Shanghai for repairs. On the seventh, it was towed to outside the Liu River Estuary. Due to strong winds at the mouth of the Yangtze River, the Jianguo ship had difficulty sailing. The iron barge was temporarily unloaded at the port of Liu River, and another ship was planned to tow it. Unexpectedly, after the Jianguo ship left for Shanghai, the iron barge was suddenly reported missing. It had probably been washed away by the wind and waves on the river to another location.

Found in Haimen 177

The iron barge was washed away by the strong winds and waves, drifting from outside the port of Liu River to the port of Haimen. At that time, the Haimen Water Police District received a report saying that a large iron barge had drifted from the sea. There was no one on board. The Water Police District took it into custody on behalf of the owner, and at the same time, it was advertised to be claimed. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received this message and urgently sent its members Shi Weijun and Zhang Huanwen to Haimen to inspect it. After reconnaissance, it was confirmed that it was the iron barge from Nanjing that had drifted away from the Liu River.

Negotiating to Retrieve 178

Shi and Zhang arrived in Haimen and contacted the Water Police District. It was said that the iron barge was found in the Songji Port. Since there was no one on board to ask, and the company name was not indicated, there was no way to notify the claim. Now that it has been proven to belong to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, it can be returned. Shi and Zhang first returned to Shanghai yesterday morning to report to the head of the shipping department, prepared an official letter to claim it, and the company negotiated with the Xinrenhe ship to tow it back to Shanghai on behalf of the company. The company also decided to heavily reward the Haimen Water Police District for taking care of the barge.

The Dispute Over Awning Licenses on Nanjing Road Has Been Settled 179

The Public Concession charges 1 yuan and 40 cents annually for awning licenses along Nanjing Road. The donation department of the Public Works Department used to send people to collect them door-to-door every summer, which was very convenient. This year, it was suddenly changed to be paid by the stores themselves, but without formal notice. Because the stores did not know about the change, they had not paid for the licenses. Then, the Laozao Police Station, without asking for the reason, suddenly accused dozens of stores on that road of violating the regulations in the Special District Court. After receiving the court summons, the stores reported in fear to the Nanjing Road Business Association. The two chairmen of the association, Wang and Sun, negotiated with the police station and learned about the situation of the change. They immediately questioned the police station for not giving formal notice in advance and should not have been so critical. The police chief shirked responsibility one by one, and there was no result. After the committee members of the association reported to the two chairmen, they were extremely angry and immediately appointed five representatives, Wang Lianfang, Sun Wenyi, Chen Duoming, Zhuang Zhihe, and Zhou Juchen, to present a letter to the Public Works Department for serious negotiations. He Dehui, the chairman, received them, and after the representatives explained, Chairman He confirmed that the police station's actions were inappropriate and promised to immediately instruct the police station to withdraw the accusations. The representatives also requested that in order to facilitate merchants, they should still send people to collect the fees as usual in the future. Chairman He has also agreed. It is heard that the accusations have now been withdrawn by the police station, and a crisis has been settled.

Russian Lai Weisi Ji and Labor Fanuofu, etc., on March 28th of this year, pretended to be the French Deputy Consul and the French Consul General at the Dentomo Hotel in the Public Concession, wanting to work on establishing a gambling den in the French Concession for Xu Haidu, and the fraud was unsuccessful. A Guest Hangs Himself in the Hongxiang Hotel 182

Wang Zhilin, 51 years old, from Changzhou, lived at No. 4 Tailai Lane, Gordon Road. Yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m., Wang was eating watermelon in his room. After finishing, he placed the remaining watermelon seeds in a basket and took them to the balcony to dry. Accidentally, he fell from the balcony, his skull shattered upon impact, and his brains spilled out in a gruesome scene. The police sent a patrol car to Renji Hospital, but due to the severity of his injuries, he died before receiving treatment. The body was sent to the coroner's office for examination.

Shanghai Bar Association Forwarded Petition

Appeal Letter from Prisoners in Jintan County Prison 187

The Shanghai Bar Association submitted a letter to the Jiangsu Higher Court, stating that it was forwarding an appeal letter from prisoners in Jintan County Prison and requesting an investigation. The letter stated, "Our country's prison administration has been notorious for its darkness. Now that the revolution has succeeded and the whole country is working to build a foundation for the rule of law, prison administration has begun to look promising. However, prison duties are detailed and complex, and few wise people are willing to try them easily. Therefore, some corrupt elements inevitably lurk within. They have no experience or knowledge and only know how to be despotic and enrich themselves. Prison reform has encountered a major obstacle. Recently, the prison warden of Jintan County Prison, Zhan Qiulai, has been pursuing his private desires and flaunting his lewd power since taking office, considering cruelty as competence and enlightenment as a wrong path. He uses deceptive tricks as sacred scriptures and follows the ashes of stubborn evil as norms. He also deducts prisoners' rations and exploits public funds, ignoring the life and death of prisoners. The dark, sunless prison administration of the feudal era has reappeared today. Beatings are worse than the three wooden punishments, and prolonged hunger is added to the punishment of axes. The suffering compatriots in Jintan County Prison have experienced all of this. The Ministry of Justice has clearly stated that prisoners' rations should be made public and the treatment of prisoners should be improved. However, the warden obeys superiors in appearance but disobeys in reality, and when dealing with subordinates, he evades the issue. If prisoners show any dissatisfaction, he can easily accuse them of plotting rebellion, making it difficult for them to advance or retreat. The undersigned (names withheld) have gathered evidence and filed a complaint with the Ministry, but considering that they are prisoners with limited power and that cunning people are prone to distorting the truth, they humbly beg that the association, which is known for upholding humanity and helping the needy, will send a telegram of assistance to alleviate this desperate situation. If the association turns a blind eye, the prisoners will be devastated. Where justice lies, how can you bear to stand idly by? The letter also hopes to be published in the newspaper so that the whole country will know that even in this era of clear rule of law, there is still a rampant warden in Jintan County, and there are still dozens of prisoners suffering in Jintan County. Moved by righteous indignation, they jointly call for an attack, so that this small place will not be forever abandoned outside the truth. This is their earnest hope." The letter was submitted to the 170th joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committee of the association, which resolved to forward it to the Jiangsu Higher Court and request it to investigate the matter. It is appropriate to submit this letter to request the court's review and implementation for the public good.
