Praying for Rain Brings Rain 275

— Wei

Recently, drought has plagued various places. Jiangnan and Zhejiang have had no rain for over a month. Although there have been a few showers in the past few days, they have been insufficient. It can be said that prayers have been answered.

Drought, drought, drought is afflicting various places. Following the drought, there are rituals to welcome the gods and set up altars to pray for rain. Especially in Shanghai, up to the day before yesterday, there were over five or six major venues set up to pray for rain. These were all presided over by prominent figures. I believe there are many other prayer gatherings that are not known. Everyone at these venues is sincerely praying for rain, hoping that their sincerity will move the heavens to send down abundant rain. This is not unique to China; even the United States, known for its scientific and material civilization, is now practicing a ban on slaughtering animals to pray for rain. This cannot be said to be a strange thing.

However, it is not really that strange. The modern capitalist civilization, which developed because of modern industry, has reached the point of declaring bankruptcy today. The destruction of capitalism has caused all the ideologies built upon it to shake. As capitalist civilization shakes, it has to return to the ancient family of religion, asking religion for help, giving it a mystical facade. Religion was originally strongly opposed by capitalist civilization, but that was when capitalism was in its prime. Now that capitalism is old and weak, it needs religion to help it. Without the help of religion, it really cannot linger. That is why praying to the gods for rain is also prevalent in the United States today. As the saying goes, "When people are poor, they call on heaven; when they are sick, they call on their parents." This is a futile measure.

As for China's prayer for rain, although it is an old method passed down for thousands of years, it was clearly ineffective in recent years. The continuous destruction of temples in various places in the past few years is one example. Recently, this idea of using gods to teach has been revived. The revival of things like religious gatherings and welcoming-the-gods festivals, as well as the recent prayer for rain in various places, have all been innovated and turned into one of the social and cultural movements of recent years. This is not without meaning. Although this meaning is different in degree from the use of religion by capitalist civilization, its essence is not very different. This is why superstition has been particularly rampant in China in recent years, and where it comes from.

Historically, abrupt changes are approaching day by day. As a result, all anti-scientific ideals are flourishing more and more. But this anti-scientific ideal will certainly not stop the progress of science in the end. This is undoubtedly true. Do not say that praying for rain brings rain, and that the gods have supreme authority.

Escaping the Heat 276

— Fei

The weather is really hot! The sun is so scorching; it's unbearable. Let's all go on a heat escape trip!

Yes, it's hot, let's go on a heat escape trip: Laoshan in Qingdao, Moganshan in Hangzhou, Lushan and Guling in Jiangxi, Putuo in the South China Sea, etc., are all famous summer resorts. There, one can find the footprints of dignitaries and the tracks of gentlemen.

Going on a heat escape trip is a privilege enjoyed only by the noble and the bourgeois. The laboring masses, who are oppressed by life every day, do not have this privilege, especially poor guys like me who cannot eat their fill or keep warm! I can forget about having this opportunity.

Heat is for everyone, but of course, a few wealthy classes and high officials are exceptions. Even I am equally afraid of the heat. Watching others go on heat escape trips and stay in air-conditioned rooms makes me a little jealous. So, I made a great vow to the heavens, gritting my teeth, and I wanted to try the taste of escaping the heat. Going to Lushan or Moganshan is beyond my means: a poor guy's year of sweat and blood is not enough to cover a month's worth of heat escape. This kind of unrealistic dream will never come true. Dreaming into the distant future is still a dream!

So, where was I going to go? This question kept swirling in my mind. As a result, after several days and nights of thinking, I finally decided to run to the countryside to escape the heat. Summer in the countryside may be better than in the city, with a quiet environment and fresh air, but without the noise, dust, and alluring sounds of the city.

Now, I have temporarily left the life in the city and escaped to the countryside, which the great gentlemen are unwilling to go to, to spend the summer. When this summer is over, I will return to the city. There, I would like to write some random notes about rural life. Perhaps, in these notes, I can tell some strange stories and ordinary news to the people in the city. Goodbye! People in the city! I wish you eternally sipping that pink wine.

Only two days after I returned to the countryside, my friend Shen Junlvping wrote a letter to me. He said in his letter:

"Xiafei: Are you happy living in the mountains? Since I came to Shanghai, it has been two weeks. But in my dreams, I still often miss Shigong. The inscriptions on the wall, I will wait until next year when the peach blossoms bloom to enjoy them with you again.

Living deep in the forests and springs, without the noise of carriages and horses, with the joy of mountains and rivers, secular thoughts are washed away, and the mind is open. It is no wonder you always envy the countryside and hate the city. What I hate is that we are driven by hunger and cannot help ourselves. We work hard all day long, relying on others to make a living, and we cannot enjoy this pure happiness in the world..." (This spring, I traveled with him to Shigong. His article was published in the "New Shanghai" section of the Shishi Xinbao. This time I returned to my hometown, and he happened to come to Shanghai only two weeks ago.)

Indeed, playing with the children during the day and lying by the south window at night, drinking three cups of wine when there is nothing to do, and leisurely reciting the poems of the ancients, this situation is no less than that of the ancient Emperors. I think the masses in the city cannot enjoy this kind of pure happiness.

Life in the countryside is regulated, and it can even be said to be mechanized. Although I have only been in the countryside for three short days, I have deeply felt its boundless charm.

Therefore, before sunrise or in the shadows of the setting sun, by the lake and in the woods, my footprints often appear.

Ghosts and Gods 277

— Juefu

Perhaps it is because we were born in the most scientifically advanced twentieth century, and everyone has been somewhat touched by the baptism of science, so we always think that people who piously pray to the gods to eliminate disasters and bring blessings are the most ignorant! We use science as the basis to oppose superstition in ghosts and gods, and of course no one dares to question this. However, human beings are, after all, a product of philosophy. People are always seeking an explanation for everything in the universe (whether theological or scientific), and people's souls are always seeking a home. Even a person who is perfectly clear that there are no such things as ghosts and gods in the world will often think of ghosts and gods when they are at their wit's end and have no way out. A revolutionary leader, when frustrated or unable to handle things, and unable to trust himself, will often seek divination to determine good or bad fortune (according to reports, Hitler recently consulted with fortune tellers); a famous scientist, when seriously ill and all medicines are ineffective,

Page 18

if people pray to God to bless him, he will be comforted, which is the same reason.

We Chinese, as everyone knows, have always been very tolerant of foreign religions. Many foreign heresies cannot stand their ground in their birthplace, but once they are imported into China, they can become popular everywhere without hindrance. People only think that China has always taken a "broad-minded" attitude, so that is why there are such results. In fact, the miserable lives of the Chinese people are indeed a major reason.

Recently, due to the disastrous drought and heat, and the resulting epidemic, welcoming the gods to pray, and banning slaughter to pray for rain has again become prevalent everywhere. A group of people living in foreign buildings and eating big meals only criticize people's ignorance and lament deeply: "China will not perish, what is the reason for this!" However, seeing the rice seedlings, which are fattening, withering in the scorching sun, and having no way to provide relief, who would not be anxious? Watching one strong comrade after another collapsing and dying in the scorching sun, and there is no hospital willing to provide accommodation and treatment, who would not be panicked? If they do not even have a little hope in ghosts and gods, they will either sit and die anxiously, or change their ways!

Sister's Letter 278

— Jing Jia

Dear Brother:

Now I'm starting to regret it! Why did I come to school? I especially shouldn't have left my loving mother and beautiful hometown to study in this wicked city!

Brother, my environment is terrible! In my class, there are thirty-four people, only five of whom are girls. The twenty-nine male classmates are like robbers! They don't know what they think we are! Not only are the classmates in my grade like this, but the classmates in other grades are also the same. Especially me, they seem like they want to swallow me whole. They are truly cruel to me!

During the first few days of school, I was able to study peacefully, but after a week, all the classmates gradually started paying attention to me! During class, they always stared at me, quietly talking about me. It was even worse after class. I couldn't escape their frightening gazes for a moment. Brother, I'm really scared! I never imagined that things like this would happen at school. If I had known, I would never have dared to come to school.

Later, they not only stared at me with terrifying eyes, but they were always looking for a chance to get close to me. Sometimes, if I dropped a pencil, they would scramble to pick it up for me, respectfully hand it to me, and even smile at me. (I'm really scared of their smiles!) During exams, they would send me all the answers they had completed, one by one. Brother, what does this mean? Don't they want me to be able to answer the questions on my own? Also, they don't call me by my name, nor do they call me "woman" or "Miss," but they call me "Angel." Brother, what does "Angel" mean? Do you understand? Alas, I really don't know what's going on!

After that, some people even started writing me letters, using colorful paper and writing in neat fountain pen, with at least three pages per letter. There were many words I couldn't understand, mostly compliments, and they all hoped to be friends with me. At first, I really didn't know what to do. Really, brother, aren't I fifteen years old? I've never encountered anything like this before! Later, I thought it wouldn't hurt to make friends, so I wrote them back. Who knew that the letters would increase day by day? Every day when I passed the gatehouse, I could get at least ten letters. What am I supposed to do? I can't write letters all day long! And I simply don't want to read some of the letters, all full of "My dear," "Beautiful little bird," and other nauseating words. Finally, I decided to ignore them all, burning every letter that came without even looking at it. Brother, isn't that a good idea? Who knew that the letters would only increase? Some scolded, some begged, some attacked... Later, they even brazenly made a scene on the bulletin board! Alas, I dare not even think about it! As I write this letter, my hands are still shaking, my heart is still pounding, and I can no longer hold back my tears!

Brother, how can you expect me to study peacefully! Now summer vacation is here again, but what have I gained in these six months? Alas, I truly want to cry but have no tears, want to laugh but have no voice!

Brother, my dream of studying is shattered. I don't want to go to school anymore. School is simply a man-eating demon! I'd rather be with my beloved mother in my sweet hometown than run to the city to see the demon's gaping maw!

Brother, I never expected studying to be like this!

Your sister,

— Wang Zuo

A Stream of Nonsense 279

— Wen Gai

Literary works are like a piece of clothing. Those who focus on the ideological content say the fabric should be of good quality, durable, and fit well; those who focus on technique and form say the fabric should be beautiful, and the style should be fashionable and pretty. The result is: beautiful and fashionable clothes appeal to the general public; whether they are durable or not, people don't care at all, and the literary theorists who focus on technique and form triumph, making the literary theorists who focus on ideological content angrily scold the readers as "unworthy of being taught." In fact, clothes that are both of good quality and durable, and also fashionable and beautiful, appealing to both aspects, are even more popular. Isn't it the same with literary works?

Today's literary writers are just like apprentice tailors: they have to make clothes to make a living. And some are still churning out shoddy work, cutting corners.

Writers who haven't made a name for themselves write with the flourish of dragons and phoenixes, completing their work in an instant, even finishing a novel of hundreds of thousands of words in three days; writers who have become famous, however, find their inspiration dried up, unable to write even a short essay in three days. Works by writers who haven't made a name for themselves are unwanted, while writers who have become famous still can't deliver their pre-arranged articles. As a result, the market price of savage heads becomes more and more expensive, and the resentment of unknown writers soars to the sky.

Both contributors and editors are people who suffer no small amount. It is certainly bitter for contributors to have their manuscripts rejected, but it is even more bitter for editors to have no good manuscripts to edit!

Amateur Mailbox

Love and Marriage 280

— Editor

Dear Editor:

You are a good mentor in society. You always answer our difficult problems with good and beautiful methods, so I admire you very much.

Now I have a difficult matter to ask you for help with. Please reply as soon as possible. The matter is as follows:

I have a friend named Wang, who is around twenty years old and currently working as a trainee at a foreign firm. Two months ago, through a friend's introduction, he met a girlfriend named Jiang, who is currently studying at a certain elementary school. She has an elderly mother with white hair and an older brother at home, and no one else. Her family is very old-fashioned, but her mind is the opposite of her family, and she is very sociable.

Since they were introduced by a friend, they have been in harmony with each other, and there is a "feeling of regretting not having met sooner." They are often seen in movie theaters and parks.

Not long ago, her affair was discovered by her older brother. Although my friend has not had any physical relationship with her, her family is old-fashioned and made the following demands: "My friend must agree to make her his lifelong partner (marriage), or he must compensate for damages to her reputation," etc. My friend's family is also old-fashioned, so he cannot make his own decisions about his marriage, and he currently lacks the ability to support himself. In this dilemma, I implore you, sir, to help resolve this matter and list the four questions below:

(1) Should he agree to the marriage proposal?

(2) After agreeing, how can he get his family to approve of the marriage request?

(3) If he does not agree and her family resolves the matter through legal means, will he be guilty of any crime, and will the introducer be guilty?

(4) If he does not agree, what methods can he use to continue interacting with her?

Please answer the above questions in detail, one by one. I wish you good health and peace,

Respectfully, Yan Ying

Answer: Marriage is the destination of love, so when a man and woman are about to embark on the path of love, they should consider in advance whether there is a possibility of marriage in the future. It is most dangerous to blindly pursue love if there is no possibility. Your friend did not consider in advance whether he had the qualifications to independently discuss marriage. He only saw that free love was fashionable and rashly followed suit. Now he has gotten himself into trouble, and I cannot help but say that he is too muddled. Moreover, when a man and woman are passionately in love, they will inevitably seek marriage. If there are obstacles to marriage, they must do everything in their power to overcome them. There is absolutely no such thing as hesitating and wavering when hearing someone urge them to get engaged. Because of this point, I strongly suspect that your friend's love for Miss Jiang is only the pursuit of sexual love, without the sincerity of emotional love. Therefore, I originally wanted to throw the letter you wrote on his behalf into the wastebasket and ignore it; especially the fourth question, which is the most absurd. But then I thought that your friend is only a young man of about twenty years old, with little experience in dealing with the world. If I do not point out a proper way for him and let him do things in a confused manner, the situation will definitely get worse and worse, and I am afraid that there are not a few people who have this kind of problem. So I specifically decided to give a public answer.

I think your friend should quickly decide on his own course of action based on the following principles: First, he should carefully reflect and observe whether he truly loves that lady and whether that lady is his ideal partner. If so, he should agree immediately without hesitation. On the one hand, he should also communicate with his family. Even if the communication fails, it does not matter, because marriage is his own business, and after adulthood, he has the right to decide for himself, without the need for family consent. If not, the previous relationship only arose from sexual love, then he should break off cleanly from now on. Your friend has had no physical relationship with the lady, so he is not guilty of any crime. However, because your friend does things in a very unreliable manner, I must give one final piece of advice, which is that if he agrees to the other party but his family does not approve, he should always remember the responsibility he will have to bear for his family in the future and quickly find a way to become self-sufficient.

Novel

Return (6) 281

— Written by Bulgarian Ivan Vazov, Translated by Yang Sen

The two children stood as if rooted to the ground. Several hours had passed. The wind blowing from the mountains became more fierce; it whipped the children's faces and fluttered their clothes. Snow whirled around them, but they did not flinch. Their faces remained fixed on the horizon, hoping to find a living soul. Suddenly, China's heart leaped. In the distance, a troop of cavalry could be seen galloping towards them. How many soldiers there were! Surely her older brother was among them! She waited motionless. The men rode swiftly past, noisily passing the children by, continuing on their way.

China waved at two soldiers at the rear of the troop:

"Captain!" she cried, her voice full of tears. "Has our brother come?"

The two officers stopped, looking at her in surprise.

"Who is your brother?" one of the officers asked.

"Brother Stoyan, our brother Stoyan," Raducho cried impatiently, wondering how the dignified officer could not know that Stoyan was their brother.

"What Stoyan?" the officer asked.

"Stoyan from the city of Weitlun," China replied firmly.

The officer whispered a few words to his companion, then asked again with interest, "Is your brother in the cavalry?"

"Yes, yes," the poor child replied, not understanding the question.

"Oh, he's not with us, my poor child. Go home quickly. You'll freeze to death here," the other officer said.

Then, spurs clattering, the two men galloped to catch up with their troop.

China wept, Raducho lamented. Their limbs were numb with cold, their lips had completely lost all sensation. Before them stretched the road back to their village, desolate and forlorn. The people who had come to welcome the returning soldiers had now gone home. Darkness fell, and the wind grew ever more violent. They could only see the cavalry troop galloping away in the distance, the soldiers' joyous songs carried to the children's ears by the wind.

China and Raducho turned back towards the village.

Night had fallen. Hands thrust deep into their pockets, the two children walked in silence, imagining their mother waiting by the door.

The sound of a carriage drawn by three horses rose up behind them.

"Sir, are there any more soldiers coming behind?"

But the carriage sped on, and no one saw or heard them in the darkness.

Snow continued to swirl around them. This snow came from the west, from the battlefield, where the white shroud had already covered Stoyan's grave in the vineyards near Pirot?

Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

A Western Star's Determination to Change His Style) Continued 282

— Su Yin

Why was Tom Keen willing to listen to a stranger, Kin Vidor, and rashly give up his status as a red-hot star, his high salary, and risk great danger to accept that contract and leave Hollywood? This is certainly a rare thing in Hollywood, which worships money—not just money, but hard cash—but he believed it was right, so he did it. His courage is admirable. Moreover, after a year, he returned to Hollywood as a new man with a new style. He was no longer the reckless ranch hero of the past, but an actor with artistic flair. It must be said that his previous decision was wise, because the style of Western films had reached its twilight, and he had to change his course to survive.

When Kin Vidor met him, he said, "I have a plan: if you're willing to gamble with me, we can gamble... if you feel that your film career needs to start over, this is your chance. You can discuss with the company and buy back the contract. I can guarantee you a leading role in my new film. Furthermore, I can pay you a decent salary until I'm ready to start production." Tom asked, "How long will that take?" Kin Vidor said, "Probably a year. During this year, I don't care where you go or what you do, as long as you leave Hollywood and forget about the studio. You can mingle with real men and women and wash the taste of Hollywood out of your mouth! Erase the thoughts of Hollywood from your mind. First, don't think about Westerns. Also, don't worry about contracts and money. Don't be afraid that people will forget you. Because my intention is for them to forget you. You can learn some acting skills, go on stage for a while. The rest of the time, you can read, rest, and have fun. When the time comes, I'll call you. Then you'll be my star."

The average movie star would never give up a stable position, a reliable future, and a large salary for a small salary for a year, with the film's production still uncertain. But Tom Keen decided to accept Kin Vidor's plan. Within a month, he bought back his contract with the company, rejected all other contracts, and quietly went east. Because he wanted to get far away from Hollywood, he ran to a small town in the far northeast corner of Maine. That small town had a summer theater troupe. That troupe was a gathering place for national stage stars. When summer came, no matter how high their position or how great their reputation, they would come to that place and gather with stars from other regions to study and learn from each other. Their democratic spirit was very strong. Regardless of their status, everyone who performed on stage received a salary of fifty dollars a week. The purpose of the troupe was not to make money, but to establish a hub for actors to congregate. When Tom Keen arrived there, he joined the troupe, rehearsed a play, and worked hard for several months. Later, he left there and traveled all over the country, talking to various people. He strived to live in an environment close to the people and far from the Hollywood lifestyle. He said that he often worried about his future and often lay awake at night staring at the ceiling. Although he trusted Kin Vidor, much could change in a year. Perhaps Kin Vidor's business would fail and he would not be able to fulfill the contract; or perhaps he would be run over by a car, and everything would be over. However, when a year had just passed, Kin Vidor sent him a telegram, calling him to start working, which was the happiest thing he had ever experienced.

As for why he was willing to make such a decision and accept Kin Vidor's proposal, he also had his reasons. The following is what he said himself: "Before Kin Vidor contacted me, I had already been thinking about leaving Hollywood. Kin Vidor simply helped me make the decision. I believe that if a person discovers that they are not on the right path, they should have the courage to sacrifice everything to correct it. Of course, that always means giving up something stable and gambling on the future. I'm not saying that leaving a stable position is painless. At the time, I felt the pain as if I were having a tooth pulled; but if a tooth is decayed, who can bear not to pull it out? At that time, my Western films were still popular, but I always felt that the future was uncertain and without any guarantee. As for the companies, they only considered this type of Western film as a temporary tool to increase their income. Although they were very accommodating to the stars of Western films, they never put any thought or money into cultivating them. They were just waiting for time to eliminate them on their own."

When Kin Vidor met Tom Keen, he had just finished his thirteenth film. But because he realized that he was not on the right path, he resolutely decided to start over, and Kin Vidor's plan only facilitated his ambition. (The End)

Film Commentary

Review of "Mandalay" 283

— Ling He

Mandalay 丨 Nanjing 丨

Regarding this film, I feel that apart from Kay Francis's excellent performance, there is nothing else worth mentioning.

Kay Francis is indeed an excellent actress. We have seen many of her starring films, and recently, from "I Found Stella Parish" to "The House on 56th Street," she plays the sorrowful and tragic heroine, deeply capturing the fragile sympathy of the audience. Especially in "The House on 56th Street," because of her own unfortunate life experiences, she sacrifices everything to protect the daughter she abandoned, and because the story is romantic, it helps her lovely success in acting.

Now, this "Mandalay" is once again seizing her sentimental personality. The screenwriter makes her escape from national ruin and family destruction, and then be abandoned by the man she loves. She has no choice but to sell her body. Although she meets a soulmate in the meantime, he is just a drunkard. However, in the end, sorrowful people sympathize with each other. When she kills that heartless man. In this process, she is deeply and realistically portrayed. This, we can find proof in very small places: for example, after she has entered Tony's room next door on the ship, Dr. Burton comes to knock on the door. When she opens the door to receive him, it seems that she should pretend to be happy, but she is still very calm, in order to express her inner grief. From these places, it can be seen that she has a deep understanding of the personality of the character in the play, although this also includes the main ingredients of the director. In addition, she looks out alone at the bow of the ship, the quiet night makes her feel sad, when she sees the doctor drinking recklessly in the bar again, she has to shake her head and sigh secretly, which fully proves that she plays the sentimental scenes very appropriately.

However, in this scene, the quiet sorrow was destroyed in the tone by the director, because from the bow of the ship at night to the front of the bar, the design of Tony's escape is interspersed with simultaneous descriptions: this aspect is a relatively tense tone, which invisibly destroys the quiet sorrow. This is, in any case, the director's lack of grasp.

In general, the director's technique is not very brilliant. We certainly cannot point out more mistakes, but it is just that he has not failed in his duties. Most American directors imagine oriental scenes in the studio, and the Burmese scenery described here is the same as the general description of China, using a kind of exotic and insulting eye, untruthfully deceiving the audience. This is fully expressed in that nightclub. Women in embroidered clothes from the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic of China are once again appearing in front of Chinese audiences in American films. These untruthful descriptions should always be a loss to artistic works, and an attached explanation of the director's shallowness. The director's cleverness is limited to the delicate handling of individual scenes, the angle of the lens, or the guidance of the actors, which are all commendable, but without a solid grasp of other more important aspects, he will never become an extremely excellent director. However, to put it back, even if such decadent romance is directed better, it may not be needed by the general active audience.

The general story has been described above. The screenwriter's choice of subject matter and even the handling of the subject matter show that his understanding of reality is very superficial. When he writes about Tony, he seems to want the audience to curse his infidelity, so he mentions incidentally that he is selling arms; this seems to expose the conspiracy of imperialists in the colonies, but we must understand that this is completely a subconscious adoption of this material as a description of Tony's improper behavior, and the same is true later when he writes about the policeman's medal hanging on the prostitute's garter, the so-called exposure of the policeman's crime is only for the impropriety of the policeman's exile of the prostitute. And the policeman's face can be bought back with ten thousand yuan. When Tony was poisoned to death by Deah, he actually had a change of heart and jumped into the sea, without making any pre-death struggle. This kind of unrealistic romantic lover makes the audience very sympathetic; although his behavior is not upright, his conscience is ultimately good. Such a contradictory expression is a common disease of general American film writers, and the author of this play is no exception.

There is one point that should be raised as a merit of the playwright, and that is that Deah casually smashed Tony's photo frame, and was slightly injured because of him, so the young doctor came to heal her wound, to symbolize their destiny. Although this is an old technique, it is still somewhat commendable.

Human Fairy Descends 284

— Lu Zhong

The night is deep. The noise has subsided, and the stars are interwoven in the sky. In the Yige Sound Studio on Bazili Road, it seems to be separated from this city, like another world. Everything is absolutely not the realm we usually see!

The Central and Golden Theaters Simultaneously Screen Films 285

Chen Yumei joined Tianyi Film Company in the 15th year of the Republic of China (1926). Her first leading role was in the film "Tang Bohu's Three Smiles," where Ms. Chen played Qiu Xiang. She was only sixteen years old at the time, petite and clever, fitting the character's identity well, completely different from the current style. The film, in two parts, totaling twenty reels, will premiere at the Central Grand Theater on Six Ma Road starting from the 25th. Also, Ms. Chen's comedic detective film "Night Pearl," co-starring the late comedic star Zhou Kongkong, will also premiere at the Golden Grand Theater on the same day.

Submission Guidelines for the Shen Bao Film Special Issue 286

This publication is a film publication dedicated to supporting cultural promotion and art. We welcome submissions from external sources. Remuneration for published works is generous.

Once a text is published and remuneration is paid, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

The language of this publication is primarily modern Chinese, and new-style punctuation must be used. If the submission is a translation, the original text should be attached. English words should be avoided where possible.

Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper, or use carbon paper, and do not use a pencil.

This publication has limited space, so strive for brevity. Each submission should be limited to around 500 words.

Each submission must be stamped with a seal, otherwise, it will be considered unpaid.

This publication is not responsible for preserving or returning texts, photographs, etc., unless prior notice is given and a stamped, self-addressed envelope is included.

Submissions that are simultaneously submitted to other publications or are plagiarized, or that are mere reproductions of descriptions, will not be remunerated if discovered.

Film Novel

Twentieth Century (8) 287

— Wen Yin

Lilian exclaimed again, "Immortal?" Her momentary excitement vanished. She said, "I'd rather die and rot. What I need is a responsible manager. Max Jacobs is getting on the train in Cleveland. I'm going to sign a contract with him." The name Jacobs was unbearable for Jifu. He was once his servant, and now he's a successful producer! He couldn't help but shout, "Max Jacobs! He's a thief! He's an illiterate ignoramus! He can't even write his own name." Lilian laughed wildly, "He writes very well on checks, and very large checks at that!" Jifu roared, "Oh, so all you want is money!" He shook his head with a disdainful air. "You've changed, become a mercenary. But if you want money, I can give it to you too. There's a Mr. Clark, a pill tycoon, who has agreed to bear all financial responsibility, and without limitations!" He ran out and shouted to O'Malley across the hall, "O'Malley, bring that contract here."

The contract was so good that Lilian read it with mixed feelings of doubt and belief. She smiled. Ten thousand dollars paid upfront upon signing the contract… a special dressing room, completely decorated with plain white velvet… a new car, a chauffeur, a maid, a secretary, and everything else, too numerous to mention, some within her dreams, some beyond. O'Malley pointed to each detail, "Honey flows there, sign here quickly." He smiled and handed the fountain pen to Lilian, saying, "This isn't just signing a contract, it's a coronation ceremony. Boxes of jewels, thick carpets to grace your beautiful feet, marble bathtubs, crowds of servants waiting for your call." But Lilian still hesitated, and hesitated for too long. A sudden great commotion broke out in the hallway outside. The train had just arrived at the Cleveland station, and the so-called millionaire, Mr. Clark, saw his nephew coming to pick him up, and suddenly went mad again. The train conductor behind Clark, pushing and shoving him, shouted for him to get off the train. Jifu went out to take a look and couldn't help but rage, "What are you doing? This is Mr. Clark, the former pill tycoon." The conductor said, "I don't know anything else, I only know he's crazy." When Lilian heard this, an expression of extreme panic appeared on her face. She knew she had been deceived again. But the conductor, seeing her panicked expression, quickly explained, "Miss Garland, you don't need to be afraid. He's not dangerous at all... He's quite pitiful. They locked him in an asylum for over a year, but he escaped." The madman suddenly shook off the conductor. He desperately ran forward in the hallway. The conductor, Clark's nephew, and many attendants chased closely behind. Lilian retreated into her room, slammed the door shut, and said fiercely to Jifu, "This is the last time I will speak to you. I have never been so insulted!" Jifu pleaded, "My love, please listen to me. I was also deceived." Lilian turned away and ignored him. At this moment, Max Jacobs had boarded the train to see her. When she saw him, she happily shouted. She shouted a series of affectionate names: "Maxie, Max, my heavenly angel, my darling!" Max said, "I've already booked you for a Samuel Sherman play. My darling, as soon as we get off the train tomorrow, we'll go straight to the lawyer to sign the contract." (To be continued)
